text:
YUMMY cookies!!! I followed the recipe exactly, however I used 1/2 cup shortening and 1/2 cup butter. For those of you who buy the extra large jars, the measurement for an 18 ounce jar of peanut butter is "1 7/8" cups (just measure two cups and subtract 2 tablespoons). I just use the entire two cups instead. The recipe is "forgiving" with regards to the quantity of peanut butter...give or take a few tablespoons (in my book, more is better)and they always come out delicious!!! DO NOT OVERBAKE! DO NOT WAIT FOR THE EDGES TO BROWN!! Take them out once they no longer look wet and leave on cookie sheet for at least ten minutes. TY Kevin for the recipe!!!!

text:
I made these using creamy peanut butter and no nuts and they were gone in 2 days! I used a fork dipped in sugar (as suggested by a previous reviewer) to flatten them slightly, and then sprinkled them thoroughly with mini chocolate chips. I baked about 10 minutes on parchment paper so I didn't have to deal with greasy cookie sheets, and they came out perfect-- soft and chewy, just like the ones you pay $1.00 for at the mall. I'm making more today!

text:
These cookies were simple to make.  Best peanut butter taste of any I've had, outside of my mother's. And they taste better the longer they sit.  I didn't have an 18 oz jar, so I used a 16 oz jar of crunchy, and I didn't have a 3rd egg for the egg white.  I rolled these into 2 logs, and froze them for 30 - 45 minutes, until firm.  I cut them thick and baked them for 20 mins at 375.

text:
Like others, I was looking for an amazing pb cookie recipe and chose this one based on reviews. I must have a different concept of "chewy" than the author, because although I would say they were moist, they certainly weren't chewy. The dough was very crumbly and the finished product was the same. It sort of disintigrated in your mouth - almost reminded me of a super moist shortbread if that makes any sense. Obviously with a whole jar, it had good pb flavor, but the texture was definitely lacking. Forgettable recipe. I continue my search for the ultimate pb cookie. UPDATE: found my favorite - it's the Peanut Butter Chews recipe on the King Arthur Flour site.

Blow your peanut butter lovin' friends away.   These are sublime, when properly baked.  You must chill the dough.  You must know your oven.  12 minutes is right for mine.  No chill=flat, overcooked=dryish, undercooked=bendy, done right=gone in 60 seconds.

text:
I would've given this 5 stars for the delicious, most yummy peanuty buttery burst of flavor.  No pb cookie has a better, more robust flavor.  Unfortunately, these cookies (most of them) were so very soft I could bend them in half & make a sandwich.  Plus most very flat.  Now I have been baking for years & consider myself an excellent baker.  I so much wanted to love these cookies after reading the reviews, and I do love the flavor, but not the texture.  The texture ruins it for me--to the point of not wanting to make them again.  First I made very small ones(walnut size? Really?? ) and baked 10 min.  That batch was rather dry & the bottom was starting to turn dark brown.  I normally make all my cookies rather large, so next batch tried making larger at 10min.  Those turned flat like pancakes and very soft(bendable).  Medium size, hardly pressed with the fork tines at 10 min. looked about the best.

Excellent cookies!  I have been looking for a soft, moist peanut butter cookie recipe for a long time and this recipe has ended my search. text:
Wow - During the holidays, I was on the hunt for a good Peanut Butter Cookie recipe. EUREKA!!!!!  I did make some changes, but basically followed the recipe.  I always use bread flour for my cookies (the same amount) if you like a softer/chewier cookie.  If you are using a stand mixer, I don't let the butter soften too much, about 20 - 30 minutes at room temp.  I skewed the white sugar to brown sugar ratio 1/2 cup white, and 1 1/2 brown, adds chewiness.  Another reviewer said she added peanut butter chips, - WOW.  My nephew couldn't stop eating these, he just kept saying "... it's like heaven in my mouth!"  That's all assurance that this recipe is a keeper!

text:
Ok, so there are a lot of mixed reviews about this recipe.  I think the reason why it gets so many mixed reviews is because people like different types of cookies.  Here is my description.  This recipe yields very rich, very peanut buttery cookies that are more "fall apart" than chewy.  They will come out soft if you cook them a little underdone.  If you cook them too long, they will be crunchy and buttery like a shortbread type cookie.  If you are looking for chewy cookies like you find at the mall or grocery store, use Mrs. Siggs recipe from this site with a little more peanut butter.

text:
AMAZING peanut butter cookies! The secret really is not to overbake these. A few tips I've found to be helpful: Don't be shy about taking them out early because they harden up as they cool.  To save money, use chunky peanut butter instead of buying chopped peanuts.  Microwave leftover cookies for 30 seconds to replicate the soft/just baked taste and consistency!  You can also include a slice of sandwich bread in the bag with the cookies to keep them soft!

text:
I chose this recipe because I had a jar of natural peanut butter that I needed to use up or dispose of (the texture is NOT the same as regular peanut butter). And I'm so glad that I did!  I omitted the egg yolk and peanuts in the batch that I made and they still turned out awesome. Also, I followed the advice of another reviewer by microwaving the jar of peanut butter for about 30 seconds in order to soften it before adding to the batter.   All of my cookies are soft and have a great  chewy texture. Using the entire jar of peanut butter ensures cookies full of PB flavor. All in all,  Kevin gets an A+ for this recipe IMO.

text:
Very good!  A little tricky to get just right.  Don't be concerned if they look not done when they come out of the oven.  They will firm up on the pan while cooling and more when they finish cooling on the wire rack.  They are still very soft cookies.  Follow the author's advice that they should look just barely dry on the top when done -- if golden on the edges they will be overdone.  I used macadamia nuts instead of chopped peanuts but couldn't really taste them for the peanut butter dominates.  The 1/2 tsp. salt isn't necessary as there is plenty of salt in the peanut butter and the nuts.  Fine cookies for any peanut butter freak!  I give a 4 just because they are a bit tricky in the baking process.

text:
These cookies are unbelievably good!  I used a jar of creamy peanut butter (JIF) and left out the additional nuts.  I found baking them for 11 minutes, then giving them 2 minutes on the cookie sheet before removing them to a cooling rack made them come out soft and delicious.  I also only refrigerated for 1 hour, then I rolled them into balls, rolled the balls in granulated sugar, THEN flattened with the fork.  Perfect.  For added sinfulness, I dipped each one halfway into some melted chocolate almond bark.  I have received SO many compliments and requests for the recipe.  It's a keeper!

text:
A perfect cookie every time if you keep a few things in mind. The brand of peanut butter really matters. Jif or Skippy give the best taste, texture and appearance. The dough wants to be a little bit chilled. You don't have to leave it in overnight, but a few hours in the fridge really improves the appearance of the cookie. Also, keep a close eye on the baking time until you are comfortable with the time these take in your oven. If you overbake these, they go down to 3 stars or less.

text:
These cookies are KILLER!!!  I use this as a base for the cookies with the chocolate kiss in the center.  I use super chunky peanut butter and omit the chopped peeanuts.  I use parchment paper and carefully calibrate the oven and ONLY BAKE 9 minutes...they will look kind of raw.  They must be puffed up.  As soon as I take them outof the oven I place a Hershey kiss in the center.  Current favorite types are peanut butter; chocolate truffle; special dark chocolate.  I especially like the first two because they have a very soft "bite", so the entire experience of eating this cookie is smooth.  
I use a small cookie scoop which yields me about 80 cookies per batch.  
I always let them cool quite a bit on the cookie sheet before trnsfering them to a rack. (That is because sinice they are underbaked, they are too fragile to be moved within a few minutes of initial cooling.  Enjoy the calories!

These are the best peanut butter cookies I've ever made! They do thin out a bit...I would love to have them a little thicker, but they have such a delicious taste...crispy edges and a soft middle that it makes up for the thinness.  I used crunchy pb and 1 stick of lite margarine and 1 stick of lite butter.  I found 11 minutes to be PERFECT. text:
Follow the instructions for chilling the dough and use the 12 minute baking time if you want a delicate peanut butter cookie that is crispy around the edges and chewy in the middle. I opted for a jar of super chunky peanut butter and no additional nuts and the cookies are very nutty. Dip your fork in granulated sugar as you press the cookies down to avoid it sticking to the dough. I rated them a 4 out of 5 because they are just a tad too peanut buttery for me. I think I prefer the traditional, slightly more sturdy and crisp version I grew up with. These seem to get softer with storage time.

text:
This is the peanut butter cookie recipe for us from now on. It make a dense, chewy, almost peanut butter fudgey cookie that is divine. The only changes I made were for convenience sake: I used a jar of crunchy, all natural peanut butter - the kind you mix yourself, and omitted adding the chopped peanuts, and I always bake on parchment, so I omitted greasing the cookie sheets. The dough keeps well in the fridge for days - haven't tried freezing it yet but I will. I now double the recipe because they go so quickly. Definitely chill for a minimum of two hours. I try to chill the dough overnight for greatest ease in handling. It's hard to keep everyone's hands out of the batter bowl, though!

text:
The second time I made these, I had access to melted chocolate, so when they firmed up a bit, I dipped them in it, covering about 2/3 'rds of the cookie, let them sit on a wax papered baking sheet in the fridge for a few minutes until set.  OMG, were they good & GONE fast!  The third time I made them, my nephew dunked his (plain cookies) in jelly and had all his cousins doing the same within minutes, so we put out a "dip bowl" of whipped-up grape jelly (jelly whipped w/ a teaspoon of water to make it dippable) and arranged the cookies on a plate around that. Cool twist, delicious & also- GONE fast!  The adults loved it too, surprising to me. Summery: Excellent base PB cookie recipe that stands great alone without one other thing done to it.  But I thought I'd share what we did and/or happened with ours, anyway. (I perfer the original recipe, plain, with coffee or milk to dunk them in, personally). Thank you, Kevin!  PS- I agree with the other reviewers: DO NOT OVER BAKE!

The peanut butter cookies I grew up with (and my mom still makes)are crispy, so the soft, creamy texture of this cookie was a change for me.  My mom's cookie probably beats this one out on taste (although this recipe is really tasty itself), but I personally prefer the soft texture of this one.  I would definitely make these again. text:
These were very good.  I halved the recipe, and my "walnut sized" balls must have been on the small side, as the halved recipe made about 40 cookies.  If you make smaller cookies (for example, 12 per cookie sheet), reduce the baking time to 8 minutes.  When I cooked the first (dark) sheet for 12 minutes, the cookies were very overcooked and the bottoms burned.  8 minutes worked just perfectly in my oven.

I was searching for an exceptional PB cookie for a special treat for the kids and gave these a try based on the reviews. Unfortunately, these didn't work out for us. Followed the recipe precisely, but the cooking time seemed to be way too long, so we only left them in the oven for about 9 minutes (by appearance/texture). Even so, they were still really dry/crumbly (not the moist/chewy PB cookie we're used to), *VERY VERY* greasy (definitely not a cookie to just walk around with without a napkin! lol) and not very "peanut-buttery" at all. We tried another batch after chilling in the fridge overnight, but ended up with the same result. We'll go back to our "regular" tried and true from now on. Thanks for the recipe, though...always nice to try something new!

text:
I just made the Peanut Butter Cookies and they were grate. I used chunky style P.B. which worked good in place of the chopped panuts. As for as the stickeyness others complained about I did not have that porblem nor did i chill or freeze dough. I placed butter flav. crisco on my hands and that kept my hands stickey free. Cooking spray should work the same. The whole flattening with a fork did not please me too much I did 2 batches 1st batch flattening 2nd left in walnut size ball after bakeing both batches the unflattened batch gave a creamer thicker cookie. I baked batches at 350F for 13min. in preheated oven. one of the Best P.B. cookie's I have tasted but recipe needed a little tweaking. P.S. rolling ball of dough in suger to avoid stickeyness messes with the taste of the cookie making a rich cookie way to sweat.

text:
4-20-2018 ~These were ok, but they wont be in our Peanut Butter Cookie Hall of Fame.  Hubs generally loves every cookie that enters his mouth, but not this time.  He couldnt exactly put his finger on why, but did say they didnt have enough texture, that they were the same throughout.   I get it, and I agree. The dough was soft and moist, forecasting that the baked cookie would be too. Too soft, too moist - no chewiness, no crispiness, no crunchiness, just consistently soft from the outer edges to the center. This cookie needed some interest as well as some heft! Perhaps eliminating that extra egg yolk would help or adding a smidge more flour, maybe another 1/2 cup.  I also think it could use a little more leavener, maybe 1/2 tsp. of baking powder. But now were talking about a different recipe! This was a surprising disappointment, given its positives of using butter and twice as much peanut butter as many other recipes.

text:
BEST peanut butter cookies ever ate (after alterations).

I used a tad over 2 cups (since didn't level off top of the measuring cup w/ my knife).

I only keep self-rising on hand (so I never have to worry about adding the baking soda & salt). I only used 1.75 cups of flour leveling off the top of each measuring cup w/ my knife.

I put about 1.5 cups of the whole peanuts in a zip-lock bag & used a rolling pin to "chop"/break them up into small pieces. Ended up being a little over 1 cup of chopped peanuts, but hubby loves nuts, so I just threw the extra in (for a total of about 1.25 cups chopped nuts).

I sprinkle a tiny bit of white sugar on the tops of each cookie before putting them in the oven.

I baked these on a dark metal cookie sheet & found 350 degrees at 12 minutes to be a little TOO done (edges were turning brown which = overdone peanut butter cookie). Second batch went in for 11 minutes only & they were perfect.

We love iced cookies, so I made a simple icing (butter + powdered sugar), microwaved it a few seconds so it was runny & drizzled it over the warm cookies.  So good I cried.

NOTE: 
This is also a good batter to roll into a log and deep freeze.  Then you can just cut out single cookies a few at a time to make fresh cookies anytime you want.  (Frozen cookies need only 10 minutes to cook as long as you cut them thin enough, 11 if you cut them a little thicker.  Trial & error needed here for cook time depending on how thick you want your cookies to be.)

text:
This is a fantastic peanut butter cookie recipe! I use it all the time. Since finding it I've made a few adjustments. First being, instead of adding extra nuts at the end I used crunchy peanut butter (saves on cost, it's one less thing to remember at the store, and it doesn't add extra unnecessary salt). Secondly, I add about 3/4 cup of coconut flakes to the mixture to give the cookies a little extra zip. Beware, adding too much coconut can make it hard for the cookies to keep shape while baking and they'll just crumble to bits.

This recipe is quite tasty and makes A LOT... I am currently at 6 dozen decent sized cookies & still have enough dough for about 2 dozen more. I baked them for exactly 10 minutes on parchment paper. They came out very light in color (could be that I used light brown sugar) so I wasn't sure if they were completely done -- but as I took them off the cookie sheet, I noticed that they were a perfect golden color on the bottom. I don't think they are "chewy" necessarily (despite all the butter & peanut butter!), but they definitely have a velvety texture. PB cookies are my hubs favorite so the true test won't be until he comes home tonight!

text:
These are delicious!!! I picked this recipe since I wouldn't have to measure out peanut butter and it didn't use shortening. Some things I did different, just because it's how I cook.... -I just did 2 eggs, I didn't add the extra yolk (mostly because I couldn't figure out how.) -I didn't grease the cookie sheet. I didn't want to try to clean it off and my dad always taught me that peanut butter has enough oil as is.  -Finally I used a 1tbsp cookie scoop to keep things even and got 85 cookies. I would let them cool on the sheet about 2-3 minutes, stick it in the freezer for 5, and then get it ready again. I had a hard time keeping my dough cold, so I rolled them all at once, putting them into batches of 15 for each sheet.  I cooked mine for 12 minutes since I like them more on the barely cooked side so that the inside is still soft and doughy.  EXCELLENT RECIPE!!! Officially my new PB cookie choice!

text:
I pretty much followed the recipe to the letter.  The only thing I did different was to leave the dough in the fridge for about two and a half hours.  I also moistened my fork with water first before I flattened my dough.  I baked my cookies for the full 15 mins. and let set for about 2 minutes on the cookie sheet.  I then set them on foil topped with wax paper for another 3 mins. and finally placed them in the cookie jar.  Because they were still a little warm whn placed in the cookie jar this helped to make them chewy.  I will definitely make these cookies again my son loved them!

These cookies are the best! text:
These are quite good; moist, delicious, fulfilling! However, I made the following substitutions to remove all white sugars and flours, and to make it a "plant power"-based dessert.: 1. replaced white flour with 1/2 cup of whole wheat flour 2. replace white sugar for turbinado sugar (same amount). Lowered Brown sugar by 1/4 cup 3.replaced the eggs with ENER-G Egg replacement (per the directions on the box) 4. Replaced milk butter with veggie butter (any kind should be fine) 5. Used natural organic peanut butter (with the oil, and yes, the oil went right in. I happened to have on hand peanut butter with nuts, but smooth should be fine. The jar is an 16 oz.)  and that's it.  After I baked them (they also had to be under baked. 12 minutes seemed to be fine for my oven.)they were delicious and gone!  hope this helps anyone who is trying to eat a plant- based diet and still enjoy a great taste!

text:
I just made these today. I used the JIF crunchy and I'm actually giving them 3.5 stars because they were pretty good. They are SOFT, but definitely not CHEWY.  The outside does harden a bit after you take the cookies out (agree with everyone else on making them underdone by at least a few minutes).  When you take them out, they actually look like you didn't cook them long enough, but they are totally done and will be softer if you do it this way.  I didn't have baking soda so used baking powder. I don't know how this affected the recipe.  If you're looking for a soft cookie with a PB taste, these are it. However, I'm trying to find a crispy outside and chewier center. I read that using more brown sugar and less granulated will help and I'll let you know how this turns out.  Made a lot of cookies, close to 80 with this recipe.

The dough gets melty really quickly, so put the batter in the fridge after every batch of cookies to prevent the dough from becoming too soft.  Also, after removing dough from fridge, wait a little while (so that the dough isn't too cold) before you place it in the oven - otherwise the cookies will have darker edges.

country:

text:
These were great! I had several open jars of pb, some nearly empty, some still half full. It wasn't as fresh as a new jar would be (for sandwiches), but I didn't want to waste it, so I thought using it in cookies would be perfect.  For those who are concerned about the texture of the cookies, they are like any other cookie. Some people prefer theirs to be soft, some like them crispy on the outside and chewy at the center. This recipe will yield both types depending on cooking time and the oven. It took me a few trays to find the perfect "doneness" for me. I actually found I cooked mine longer (nearly 20 minutes) because I made them larger and wanted them to be crispy on the outside and chewy at the center.  For those who said the cookies were stale, try the old trick of putting them in an airtight container (tupperware, ziploc, etc.) with a slice of bread, and they will soften up/stay soft.  Thanks for the great recipe! I've got enough "old" pb for another batch!

text:
Very good cookies.  I'm rating them 4 stars because I couldn't get them really soft and chewy without sacrificing some color and appearance.  I used extra chunky peanut butter and added mini semi-sweet chips instead of the extra chopped nuts as suggested by other reviewers.  I formed the cookies with a #40 scoop which made them just the right size for me.  At this size and in my oven, 11 minutes left them greyish, oily on top, and soft & chewy, 12 minutes gave them a pretty light brown color and left them with a little softness but still more crispy than I prefer.  A larger cookie may have turned out softer, but for portion size reasons, I prefer not to make my cookies so large.  This recipe makes a ton of cookies, so I partially solved this problem by making one tray of greyish, soft ones for me and making the rest pretty and crispier for company  :-).  Overall, this is a keeper recipe.  Thanks for sharing!

text:
SO yummy!  Recipe as written is fabulous, but if you're lookier for something a bit healthier and thicker...  I felt the fat (butter & peanut butter) to flour ratio was quite high, so I used 1 cup of trans fat free Crisco instead of butter and increased the rest of the ingredients by 50%.  (If I'm going to the trouble of making cookies I want a BIG batch!)  Also used 1/2 whole wheat flour and 1/2 white flour and replaced 1/2 of the white sugar with Splenda.    I used Crunchy PB as suggested by some other reviewers.  The cookies came out thick and moist and really delicious.  You will never miss the extra fat.  In fact, I think it makes the cookies better.

ATTENTION peanut butter cookie aficionados:  These are the best ever.  Cooking time is vital to top quality outcome!  I followed the recipe exactly as written and realized that 30 seconds too long would change both the flavor and texture.  The first batch took 10 minutes, but less for each additional batch.  Don't wait until the edges brown...they must be immediately removed from the oven when the top looks dry.  I recomend watching them toward the end.  Better than any specilty bakery. Thank you Kevin,

text:
OH.MY.GOD!!!!  I have made a lot of cookies in my 45 years.  These are hands down the best cookies I've ever made.  I had to alter a little bit out of necessity, rather than desire.  I don't keep butter and I don't like to use margarine in cookies, I use golden Crisco and butter flavouring.  I also didn't have any vanilla (oops!) so I just used 2 tsp of butter flavour instead of 1 and 1.  I used crunchy peanut butter because that's what I buy and didn't have any nuts anyhow.  Finally, I added milk/white chocolate swirled chips because they taste good!  They came out with almost a shortbread texture to them and were simply incredible!  I will never use another PB cookie recipe!!! Thanks so much for posting it!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Definitely a keeper! This was my first time making peanut butter cookies and it came out fabulous! I made them for my boyfriend's birthday party and they were ALL eaten up :) I followed some reviewer's advice and used crunchy peanut butter instead of smooth peanut butter and the peanuts.  I followed the recipe exactly and will definitely use this one again.  One mistake I made was that I refrigerated the dough overnight...this led to the dough being kinda dry and crumbly in the morning when I baked them.  But, I just let it sit and warm up at room temperature and added a tiny bit of butter and the dough softened back up and was easy to use. I also had a problem with the dough sticking to my fork, but that too eased up when the dough softened, and I used some non-stick cooking spray on the fork.  I usually don't bake but this has provoked me to try something else soon!
Made these again on 8/7/10: be sure to stir it up well or else you'll get different batches of cookies like I did! I also used the suggestion for pressing with a sugared fork to prevent them from sticking...this worked really well and I'll do that again next time!

These are wonderful cookies! My kids and husband love them as well. Don't make them if you're on a diet though ;-) I used all natural peanut butter, the kind you have to stir, which has more of a peanut taste than the other peanut butters made w/ sugar and hydrogenated oils. I also used a little scoop to put them on my pan, then criss-crossed them w/ a fork. Bake time was exactly 8 minutes. It made 100 cookies this way! Wow!
